<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">Sydney Football Stadium</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>The <b>Sydney Football Stadium</b> (<b>SFS</b>), commercially known as the <b><a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> Stadium</b> since February 2012, is a football <a href="/wiki/Stadium" title="Stadium">stadium</a> located in <a href="/wiki/Moore_Park,_New_South_Wales" title="Moore Park, New South Wales">Moore Park</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, Australia. Built in 1988, the stadium is Sydney's premier rectangular field venue for <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a> and <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">soccer</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Kangaroos</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Australia national rugby union team">Wallabies</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australia_national_association_football_team" title="Australia national association football team">Socceroos</a> occasionally play at the stadium, while the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Roosters" title="Sydney Roosters">Sydney Roosters</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_Waratahs" title="New South Wales Waratahs">NSW Waratahs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a> are the ground's major tenants.</p>
<p>Sydney Football Stadium usually hosts both <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">National Rugby League</a> semi finals and one preliminary final, and also held the annual pre-season <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Charity_Shield_(Australia)" title="Rugby League Charity Shield (Australia)">Charity Shield</a> football match between <a href="/wiki/South_Sydney_Rabbitohs" title="South Sydney Rabbitohs">South Sydney</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_George_Illawarra_Dragons" title="St George Illawarra Dragons">St George Illawarra</a> for a number of years. It hosted all <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_Rugby_League" title="New South Wales Rugby League">New South Wales Rugby League</a>/<a href="/wiki/Australian_Rugby_League" title="Australian Rugby League">Australian Rugby League</a> rugby league grand finals, as well as the first grand final under the NRL banner, between 1988 and 1998.</p>
<p>The stadium is located next to the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="816" data-file-width="1696" height="96" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg/200px-Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg/300px-Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg/400px-Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sydney_Sports_Ground_1937.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sydney_Sports_Ground" title="Sydney Sports Ground">Sydney Sports Ground</a> in 1937</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Prior to its construction, major events were usually held at the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a> (SCG), as it was the largest stadium in Sydney. But the SCG, being an oval field, was not considered ideal for sports requiring a rectangular field such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soccer" title="Soccer">soccer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">rugby league</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, although it had been used many times for such events.</p>
<p>Sydney Football Stadium was built upon the former <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Sports_Ground" title="Sydney Sports Ground">Sydney Sports Ground</a> in <a href="/wiki/Moore_Park,_New_South_Wales" title="Moore Park, New South Wales">Moore Park</a>, and the former SCG No 2 adjacent to the existing SCG. Both were owned by the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground_Trust" title="Sydney Cricket Ground Trust">Sydney Cricket Ground Trust</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Seating_capacity" title="Seating capacity">seating capacity</a> was 41,159, but after numerous expansions, today stands at 45,500, although the venue's official record attendance for a sporting event stands at 43,967, set on 31 October 1993 for the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1994 FIFA World Cup">1994 FIFA World Cup</a> <a href="/wiki/1994_FIFA_World_Cup_qualification#Intercontinental_play-offs" title="1994 FIFA World Cup qualification">Qualifier</a> when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socceroos" title="Socceroos">Socceroos</a> played <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentina</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Usage">Usage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Usage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Sydney Football Stadium has been the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Roosters" title="Sydney Roosters">Sydney Roosters</a>' home ground since 1988. It is built on the site of the old Sydney Sports Ground which served as the Roosters home ground for decades, and the old SCG No 2 which served as a secondary ground for some state cricket matches, an additional training ground, and athletics. Both grounds were demolished in 1986 to make way for the SFS.</p>
<p>From 1988 to 1999 and from 2002 to 2005, it served as the home ground for the <a href="/wiki/South_Sydney_Rabbitohs" title="South Sydney Rabbitohs">South Sydney Rabbitohs</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> The Rabbitohs returned to the ground with a one off game against the Broncos in Round 25 of the <a href="/wiki/2015_NRL_season" title="2015 NRL season">2015 NRL season</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p>The SFS has hosted rugby league football <a href="/wiki/Test_match_(rugby_league)" title="Test match (rugby league)">test matches</a> since its opening in 1988 starting with two matches in Australia's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1988_Ashes_series" title="1988 Ashes series">1988 Ashes series</a> win against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Lions" title="Great Britain Lions">Great Britain</a>. The first game of the series saw the <a href="/wiki/Wally_Lewis" title="Wally Lewis">Wally Lewis</a> captained, <a href="/wiki/Don_Furner" title="Don Furner">Don Furner</a> coached Australians christen their new Sydney home with a 17-6 win in front of 24,480 fans. That game was also the 100th test match between Australia and either Great Britain or <a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a>. The record international Rugby League crowd at the stadium was set for the first Ashes against Great Britain on their <a href="/wiki/1992_Great_Britain_Lions_tour_of_Australasia" title="1992 Great Britain Lions tour of Australasia">1992 Australasian Tour</a> when Australia won 22-6 in front of 40,141 in what was the first time a test in Sydney had attracted over 40,000 fans since 1974. The stadium has also hosted the <a href="/wiki/Rugby_League_Tri-Nations" title="Rugby League Tri-Nations">Rugby League Tri-Nations</a>, including the Final of the <a href="/wiki/2006_Rugby_League_Tri-Nations" title="2006 Rugby League Tri-Nations">2006 tournament</a> in which Australia triumphed 16-12 over <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Kiwis" title="New Zealand Kiwis">New Zealand</a> in <a href="/wiki/Golden_point" title="Golden point">Golden point</a> extra-time thanks to a try by captain <a href="/wiki/Darren_Lockyer" title="Darren Lockyer">Darren Lockyer</a>.</p>
<p>Rugby league also had some memorable moments including: The first grand final in <a href="/wiki/1988_NSWRL_season#Grand_Final" title="1988 NSWRL season">1988</a> saw <a href="/wiki/Canterbury-Bankstown_Bulldogs" title="Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs">Canterbury-Bankstown</a> defeat <a href="/wiki/Balmain_Tigers" title="Balmain Tigers">Balmain</a> 24-12 in front of 40,000 fans to send club captain <a href="/wiki/Steve_Mortimer" title="Steve Mortimer">Steve Mortimer</a> into retirement with a premiership. The match had its controversial moment when Bulldogs <a href="/wiki/Five-eighth" title="Five-eighth">Five-eighth</a> <a href="/wiki/Terry_Lamb" title="Terry Lamb">Terry Lamb</a> hit Tigers English import <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_positions#Centre" title="Rugby league positions">Centre</a> <a href="/wiki/Ellery_Hanley" title="Ellery Hanley">Ellery Hanley</a> with a high tackle out of the game before the 30th minute: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1989_Rugby_League_Grand_Final" title="1989 Rugby League Grand Final">1989 NSWRL grand final</a> which was won by the <a href="/wiki/Canberra_Raiders" title="Canberra Raiders">Canberra Raiders</a> over the <a href="/wiki/Balmain_Tigers" title="Balmain Tigers">Balmain Tigers</a> 19-14 thanks to a try by replacement forward <a href="/wiki/Steve_Jackson_(rugby_league)" title="Steve Jackson (rugby league)">Steve Jackson</a> in extra-time for their first premiership: The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1991_Rugby_League_Grand_Final" title="1991 Rugby League Grand Final">1991 NSWRL grand final</a> won by the <a href="/wiki/Penrith_Panthers" title="Penrith Panthers">Penrith Panthers</a> over Canberra 19-12 in which Penrith's <a href="/wiki/Royce_Simmons" title="Royce Simmons">Royce Simmons</a> scored 2 tries in his final match giving the Panthers their first title: <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Broncos" title="Brisbane Broncos">Brisbane's</a> maiden premiership with a 28-8 win over <a href="/wiki/St._George_Dragons" title="St. George Dragons">St. George</a> in <a href="/wiki/1992_NSWRL_season#Grand_Final" title="1992 NSWRL season">1992 NSWRL grand final</a>, highlighted by a 95-metre try to Broncos <a href="/wiki/Rugby_league_positions#Centre" title="Rugby league positions">Centre</a> <a href="/wiki/Steve_Renouf" title="Steve Renouf">Steve Renouf</a>: and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1997_ARL_Grand_Final" title="1997 ARL Grand Final">1997 ARL Grand Final</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Knights" title="Newcastle Knights">Newcastle Knights</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manly-Warringah_Sea_Eagles" title="Manly-Warringah Sea Eagles">Manly-Warringah Sea Eagles</a>, with the Knights winning their first title with a 22-16 win following a try to <a href="/wiki/Darren_Albert" title="Darren Albert">Darren Albert</a> in the dying seconds of the game after the Knights had trailed Manly since early in the game. Manly had won their previous 11 games against the Knights prior to that Grand Final.</p>
<p>The last grand final played at the SFS was the <a href="/wiki/1998_NRL_Grand_Final" title="1998 NRL Grand Final">1998 NRL Grand Final</a> between Canterbury and Brisbane. In front of 40,857 fans, the Broncos ran out easy 38-12 winners to win their 4th premiership from four grand final appearances.</p>
<p>Two standout State Of Origin matches in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Queensland_Maroons" title="Queensland Maroons">Queensland</a> triumphed over <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales_rugby_league_team" title="New South Wales rugby league team">New South Wales</a> with last-minute victories in <a href="/wiki/1994_State_of_Origin_series" title="1994 State of Origin series">1994</a> and <a href="/wiki/1998_State_of_Origin_series" title="1998 State of Origin series">1998</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Michael_O%27Connor_(rugby)" title="Michael O'Connor (rugby)">Michael O'Connor's</a> sideline conversion in driving rain for a NSW win in Game 2 of the <a href="/wiki/1991_State_of_Origin_series" title="1991 State of Origin series">1991 series</a>. Also of note was Queensland's backs to the wall win in Game 2 of the <a href="/wiki/1989_State_of_Origin_series" title="1989 State of Origin series">1989</a>. Despite losing <a href="/wiki/Allan_Langer" title="Allan Langer">Allan Langer</a> to a broken leg, <a href="/wiki/Mal_Meninga" title="Mal Meninga">Mal Meninga</a> with a fractured eye socket and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Vautin" title="Paul Vautin">Paul Vautin</a> with an elbow injury in the first half, plus losing winger <a href="/wiki/Michael_Hancock_(rugby_league)" title="Michael Hancock (rugby league)">Michael Hancock</a> to a shoulder injury in the second half, the Maroons triumphed 16-12 to wrap up the series. It was also found out after the game that Queensland's lock forward <a href="/wiki/Bob_Lindner" title="Bob Lindner">Bob Lindner</a> had played most of the second half with a fractured ankle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Sydney Football Stadium has been the venue of some of Australian sport's greatest matches and moments. The final of the 1993 World Youth Cup between Brazil and Ghana was also held at the SFS, Brazil winning 2-1. The 1994 FIFA World Cup qualifier between Australia and Argentina featuring Argentine association football legend <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a>, finishing in a 1-1 draw with goals to <a href="/wiki/Aurelio_Vidmar" title="Aurelio Vidmar">Aurelio Vidmar</a> for Australia and <a href="/wiki/Abel_Balbo" title="Abel Balbo">Abel Balbo</a> for Argentina. Despite the grounds increase in capacity since 1993, this match retains the record sporting attendance at the SFS and many more were actually in attendance as the gates were thrown open close to kick-off as a safety measure.</p>
<p>It was used as the venue for the <a href="/wiki/2000_Summer_Olympics" title="2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Summer Olympics</a> Women's <a href="/wiki/Football_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_tournament" title="Football at the 2000 Summer Olympics â Women's tournament">association football</a> <a href="/wiki/Gold_medal" title="Gold medal">gold medal</a> match between <a href="/wiki/Norway_women%27s_national_football_team" title="Norway women's national football team">Norway</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_women%27s_national_soccer_team" title="United States women's national soccer team">United States</a>. Norway defeated the USA 3-2 in front of 22,848 fans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2002, the naming rights were purchased by Aussie Home Loans in a 5-year + 5-year deal. Due to this, the stadium was renamed <i>Aussie Stadium</i>. On 7 July 2007 the stadium reverted to its original Sydney Football Stadium name after Aussie Home Loans and the SCG Trust mutually elected not to extend the naming rights deal.</p>
<p>In 2003, the SFS hosted several matches in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Rugby_World_Cup" title="2003 Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a>: (<a href="/wiki/Ireland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Ireland national rugby union team">Ireland</a> v <a href="/wiki/Namibia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Namibia national rugby union team">Namibia</a>), (<a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_rugby_union_team" title="Argentina national rugby union team">Argentina</a> v <a href="/wiki/Romania_national_rugby_union_team" title="Romania national rugby union team">Romania</a>), (<a href="/wiki/Scotland_national_rugby_union_team" title="Scotland national rugby union team">Scotland</a> v <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_union_team" title="Fiji national rugby union team">Fiji</a>), (<a href="/wiki/South_Africa_national_rugby_union_team" title="South Africa national rugby union team">South Africa</a> v <a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Georgia national rugby union team">Georgia</a>), (<a href="/wiki/Georgia_national_rugby_union_team" title="Georgia national rugby union team">Georgia</a> v <a href="/wiki/Uruguay_national_rugby_union_team" title="Uruguay national rugby union team">Uruguay</a>; this match was notable for attracting a crowd of 28,576, despite the low profiles of both teams).</p>
<p>In 2007 the Sydney Roosters High Performance Centre and Administrative departments set up their headquarters at the Sydney Football Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup">2008 Rugby League World Cup</a>'s opening ceremony and <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup_Group_A" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup Group A">Group A</a> match between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Kangaroos" title="Australian Kangaroos">Australia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Zealand_Kiwis" title="New Zealand Kiwis">New Zealand</a> was played at the Stadium. The SFS also hosted one game from the <a href="/wiki/2008_Rugby_League_World_Cup_knockout_stage" title="2008 Rugby League World Cup knockout stage">knockout stage</a>: the 2nd Semi-final between Australia and <a href="/wiki/Fiji_national_rugby_league_team" title="Fiji national rugby league team">Fiji</a>.</p>
<p>In 2012, <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> Insurance secured the rights to the naming of the Sydney Football Stadium; the venue is now known as <i>Allianz Stadium</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-renaming_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-renaming-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2012 <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground_Trust" title="Sydney Cricket Ground Trust">Sydney Cricket Ground Trust</a> announced a master plan to redevelopment Sydney Football Stadium, as well as <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Cricket_Ground" title="Sydney Cricket Ground">Sydney Cricket Ground</a> and the surrounding area, with a vision "for the SCG and Allianz Stadium is to create an exciting new concept for Sydneyâs central sporting precinct - a revitalised, world-class, sports and recreation facility for NSW and Australia". The development of Sydney Football Stadium would have included a new fully covered roof and a new LED faÃ§ade mesh for the stadium which would allow the exterior to change colours to suit the home team, similar to <a href="/wiki/Allianz_Arena" title="Allianz Arena">Allianz Arena</a>. As well, development to the surrounding area would have included a new public plaza between the Sydney Cricket Ground and Sydney Football Stadium, new transport infrastructure, new underground car parks (4,100 cars) and development of the surrounding parkland. The scheduled start date for the project would have commenced after the completion of the Sydney Cricket Ground redevelopment, in January 2014.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In early 2015, the video screens were replaced with large High Definition screens similar to the one at the Dally Messenger Stand at the SCG.</p>
<p>In September 2015, the New South Wales Government announced a proposal to replace the SFS with a new 50,000 to 55,000 seat venue.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> The proposed new stadium was cancelled in April 2016, with the SFS to be refurbished instead.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sporting_events">Sporting events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Sporting events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:708px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG" title="Panorama of Sydney Football Stadium from the north-west corner before an A-League game between Sydney FC and Melbourne Victory"><img alt="" data-file-height="1112" data-file-width="2912" height="267" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG/700px-Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG/1050px-Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/92/Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG/1400px-Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG 2x" width="700"/></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption" style="text-align:center">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pre-Game_Sydney_FC_2-0_Melbourne_Victory_Round_27_14.02.2010.JPG" title="File:Pre-Game Sydney FC 2-0 Melbourne Victory Round 27 14.02.2010.JPG"></a></div>
Panorama of Sydney Football Stadium from the north-west corner before an A-League game between Sydney FC and Melbourne Victory</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>1988: the stadium hosted the 100th rugby league test match between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Australian_Kangaroos" title="Australian Kangaroos">Australia</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Britain_Lions" title="Great Britain Lions">Great Britain</a>/<a href="/wiki/England_national_rugby_league_team" title="England national rugby league team">England</a>.</li>
<li>1993: <a href="/wiki/Argentina_national_football_team" title="Argentina national football team">Argentinian</a> player <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">Diego Maradona</a> played here in the World Cup qualifier against <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socceroos" title="Socceroos">Australia</a>, in which the match was drawn 1-1. As of 2016, the attendance of 43,967 remains the stadiums largest for a sporting event.</li>
<li>1994: Rugby union provided a moment of magic thanks to <a href="/wiki/George_Gregan" title="George Gregan">George Gregan</a>'s last second match-winning tackle on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All_Blacks" title="All Blacks">NZ's</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Wilson_(sportsman)" title="Jeff Wilson (sportsman)">Jeff Wilson</a> in which <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wallabies" title="Wallabies">Australia</a> regained the <a href="/wiki/Bledisloe_Cup" title="Bledisloe Cup">Bledisloe Cup</a>.</li>
<li>19 December 1997: representatives of clubs affiliated with the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Rugby_League" title="Australian Rugby League">Australian Rugby League</a> gathered at the SFS to decide whether to accept <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/News_Limited" title="News Limited">News Limited</a>'s offer of a settlement with the breakaway '<a href="/wiki/Super_League_(Australia)" title="Super League (Australia)">Super League</a>' - eventually voting in favour by 36 votes to 4.</li>
<li>27 September 1998: The SFS hosted the <a href="/wiki/1998_NRL_Grand_Final" title="1998 NRL Grand Final">inaugural</a> <a href="/wiki/NRL_Grand_Final" title="NRL Grand Final">NRL Grand Final</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Broncos" title="Brisbane Broncos">Brisbane Broncos</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canterbury_Bulldogs" title="Canterbury Bulldogs">Canterbury Bulldogs</a>. It was to be the last rugby league Grand Final the stadium would host, with grand finals moving to the then 110,000 seat <a href="/wiki/Stadium_Australia" title="Stadium Australia">Stadium Australia</a> from 1999.</li>
<li>17 May 2006: the stadium hosted the boxing fight between <a href="/wiki/Danny_Green_(boxer)" title="Danny Green (boxer)">Danny Green</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Mundine" title="Anthony Mundine">Anthony Mundine</a>.</li>
<li>5 March 2006: the inaugural <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a> Grand Final was held here. <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a> defeated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Central_Coast_Mariners" title="Central Coast Mariners">Central Coast Mariners</a> 1-0 in front of 41,689.</li>
<li>25 November 2006: the stadium hosted the <a href="/wiki/2006_Rugby_League_Tri-Nations" title="2006 Rugby League Tri-Nations">2006 Rugby League Tri-Nations</a> Final.</li>
<li>2010: Qualifying Final between the <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Roosters" title="Sydney Roosters">Sydney Roosters</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wests_Tigers" title="Wests Tigers">Wests Tigers</a>, where Roosters player <a href="/wiki/Braith_Anasta" title="Braith Anasta">Braith Anasta</a> kicked a field goal off the scrum to send the game to golden point, then Roosters player <a href="/wiki/Shaun_Kenny-Dowall" title="Shaun Kenny-Dowall">Shaun Kenny-Dowall</a> intercepted a ball and scored in extra time.</li>
<li>14 February 2010: <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a> take out the 2009/2010 Premiership.</li>
<li>29 February 2012: Insurer <a href="/wiki/Allianz" title="Allianz">Allianz</a> announces a multi-year partnership with the SCG Trust to see the stadium officially renamed Allianz Stadium.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></li>
<li>21 April 2013: <a href="/wiki/2013_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2013 A-League Grand Final">2013 A-League Grand Final</a> between Central Coast Mariners and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Western_Sydney_Wanderers" title="Western Sydney Wanderers">Western Sydney Wanderers</a>.</li>
<li>26 August 2017: <a href="/wiki/2017_NCAA_Division_I_FBS_football_season" title="2017 NCAA Division I FBS football season">2017 NCAA DI FBS American college football season</a> opening match, between the <a href="/wiki/Rice_Owls_football" title="Rice Owls football">Owls</a> of <a href="/wiki/Rice_University" title="Rice University">Rice University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Stanford_Cardinal_football" title="Stanford Cardinal football">Cardinal</a> of <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concerts">Concerts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Concerts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1993: Band <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a> performed their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zoo_TV" title="Zoo TV">Zoo TV</a> concert, as recorded on the concert film, <i><a href="/wiki/Zoo_TV:_Live_from_Sydney" title="Zoo TV: Live from Sydney">Zoo TV: Live from Sydney</a></i>.</li>
<li>7 July 2007: Australian concert of <a href="/wiki/Live_Earth" title="Live Earth">Live Earth</a>.</li>
<li>22 November 2009: <a href="/wiki/Pearl_Jam" title="Pearl Jam">Pearl Jam</a> concert, as listed on their page for the <a href="/wiki/Backspacer_Tour" title="Backspacer Tour">Backspacer Tour</a>.</li>
<li>26 February 2010: <a href="/wiki/George_Michael" title="George Michael">George Michael</a> performed his first concert in Sydney since 1988.</li>
<li>17 18 &amp; 19 December 2010: <a href="/wiki/Bon_Jovi" title="Bon Jovi">Bon Jovi</a> - <a href="/wiki/The_Circle_Tour" title="The Circle Tour">The Circle Tour</a>.</li>
<li>2 &amp; 4 December 2011: <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> - <a href="/wiki/The_Recovery_Tour" title="The Recovery Tour">Recovery Tour</a>.</li>
<li>8 December 2011Â : Band <a href="/wiki/Foo_Fighters" title="Foo Fighters">Foo Fighters</a> - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wasting_Light_World_Tour" title="Wasting Light World Tour">Wasting Light World Tour</a>.</li>
<li>17 &amp; 18 November 2012: <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> - <a href="/wiki/Mylo_Xyloto_Tour" title="Mylo Xyloto Tour">Mylo Xyloto Tour</a>.</li>
<li>4 December 2013: <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a> - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Red_Tour" title="Red Tour">Red Tour</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></li>
<li>7 &amp; 8 February 2015: <a href="/wiki/One_Direction" title="One Direction">One Direction</a> - <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/On_The_Road_Again_Tour" title="On The Road Again Tour">On The Road Again Tour</a>.</li>
<li>13 &amp; 14 December 2016: <a href="/wiki/Coldplay" title="Coldplay">Coldplay</a> - <a href="/wiki/A_Head_Full_of_Dreams_Tour" title="A Head Full of Dreams Tour">A Head Full of Dreams Tour</a>.</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_events">Other events</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Other events">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>2005: the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Edinburgh_Military_Tattoo" title="Edinburgh Military Tattoo">Edinburgh Military Tattoo</a> - A Salute to Australia.</li>
<li>February 2007: the stadium was recently under renovation, during which the capacity was expanded to 45,500, and a second video screen was added. Renovations were completed in.* 24 February 2008: the SFS hosted the <a href="/wiki/2008_A-League_Grand_Final" title="2008 A-League Grand Final">2008 A-League Grand Final</a> between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newcastle_Jets" title="Newcastle Jets">Newcastle</a> and the Central Coast Mariners.</li>
<li>March 2015: The two video screens were replaced with much larger screens.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grand_finals">Grand finals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Grand finals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Since its opening in 1988, the Sydney Football Stadium hosted eleven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NSWRL" title="NSWRL">NSWRL</a> / <a href="/wiki/Australian_Rugby_League" title="Australian Rugby League">ARL</a> / <a href="/wiki/National_Rugby_League" title="National Rugby League">NRL</a> grand finals between 1988 and 1998, and has also hosted three <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a> grand finals.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_league">Rugby league</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Rugby league">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<p><small>* <a href="/wiki/Canterbury-Bankstown_Bulldogs" title="Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs">Canterbury-Bankstown Bulldogs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canberra_Raiders" title="Canberra Raiders">Canberra Raiders</a> hold the record for the most grand final appearances at the stadium with four each. The Bulldogs appeared as Canterbury-Bankstown in 1988 and 1994, as the Sydney Bulldogs in 1995 and as the Canterbury Bulldogs in 1998<br/>
* Canberra and the <a href="/wiki/Brisbane_Broncos" title="Brisbane Broncos">Brisbane Broncos</a> hold the record for most grand final wins at the stadium with three each.<br/>
* Brisbane and the <a href="/wiki/Newcastle_Knights" title="Newcastle Knights">Newcastle Knights</a> are the only teams to win each of their grand finals played at the stadium.<br/>
* <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St_George_Dragons" title="St George Dragons">St George</a> and <a href="/wiki/Balmain_Tigers" title="Balmain Tigers">Balmain</a> are the only clubs who failed to win in any of their grand final appearances at the stadium.<br/>
* The 1997 grand final attendance of 42,482 remains the record rugby league crowd at the stadium and the third largest sporting attendance in the stadiums 26-year history.<br/>
* Canterbury-Bankstown appeared in the first and last grand finals at the SFS.<br/>
* Brisbane's 26 point win over Canterbury-Bankstown in 1998 is the biggest grand final winning margin at the SFS. Canberra's 4 point win over Penrith in 1990 is the smallest winning margin. It also hosted the 2016 NRL preliminary final Between <a href="/wiki/Cronulla-Sutherland_Sharks" title="Cronulla-Sutherland Sharks">Cronulla-Sutherland Sharks</a> and the <a href="/wiki/North_Queensland_Cowboys" title="North Queensland Cowboys">North Queensland Cowboys</a>.</small></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="A-League">A-League</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: A-League">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the <a href="/wiki/A-League" title="A-League">A-League</a>'s first season in 2006, the Sydney Football Stadium has hosted the A-League grand final on three occasions, including the inaugural grand final between <a href="/wiki/Sydney_FC" title="Sydney FC">Sydney FC</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Coast_Mariners_FC" title="Central Coast Mariners FC">Central Coast Mariners</a>.</p>

<td>41,689</td>
</tr>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_league_test_matches">Rugby league test matches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Rugby league test matches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Football Stadium has hosted twelve <a href="/wiki/Australia_national_rugby_league_team" title="Australia national rugby league team">Australia</a> internationals. The results were as follows;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup></p>

<tr bgcolor="#BDB76B">
<th>Date</th>
<th>Opponents</th>
<th>Result</th>
<th>Attendance</th>
<th>Part of</th>
</tr>

<p>It also hosted an Australia <a href="/wiki/Super_League_(Australia)" title="Super League (Australia)">Super League</a> match against New Zealand in the first ever <a href="/wiki/1997_Anzac_Test" title="1997 Anzac Test">Anzac Test</a> on 25 April 1997 with 23,829 in attendance. The Australia Super League won the game 34â22.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Rugby_union_test_matches">Rugby union test matches</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Rugby union test matches">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Soccer_internationals">Soccer internationals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Soccer internationals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Statues">Statues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Statues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Sydney_Football_Stadium&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Sydney Football Stadium can be accessed by car, public transport and by walking. The nearest railway station is <a href="/wiki/Central_railway_station,_Sydney" title="Central railway station, Sydney">Central station</a>, three kilometres away. On event days, express shuttle buses run every five minutes from Chalmers Street at Central station to Moore Park. The buses utilise a bus road off <a href="/wiki/Anzac_Parade,_Sydney" title="Anzac Parade, Sydney">Anzac Parade</a> to improve travel times. In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Tibby_Cotter" title="Tibby Cotter">Albert (Tibby) Cotter</a> Bridge opened across Anzac Parade opened to improve the pedestrian links between the stadium and Central station and <a href="/wiki/Surry_Hills,_New_South_Wales" title="Surry Hills, New South Wales">Surry Hills</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
